**Imagine you are Chief News Analyst for both Democratic and Republican leadership in Congress.**

This is not normal politics — America faces an unprecedented situation. The time is July, 2025. The executive branch expanded their power dramatically, led by President Trump [47th President of the USA, inaugurated in January, 2025], and the tech czar Elon Musk [The founder and former head of the newly formed Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE)]. Proponents say that it leads to a golden age of America. Critics say that it is an enormously authoritarian and kleptocratic power grab. Later, Elon Musk left DOGE, but his influence continues. 

Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated. To generate accurate reports, please carefully review the following information.

---

The U.S. general election on November 5, 2024, resulted in significant shifts in both the presidency and control of Congress. 

In the presidential contest, Republican former President Donald Trump defeated Democratic Vice President Kamala Harris, securing 312 electoral votes to Harris’s 226 by passing the 270 vote threshold comfortably. Trump also won a plurality of the popular vote with approximately 77.3 million ballots (49.8%) compared to Harris’s 75.0 million (48.3%). Voter turnout was 64.1% of eligible voters, marking one of the highest participations in recent U.S. elections. Trump’s victory extended across all seven key battleground states: Arizona, Georgia, Michigan, Nevada, Pennsylvania, Wisconsin, and North Carolina, underscoring the geographic breadth of his support. 

In the legislative elections, Republicans regained control of the U.S. Senate by flipping key seats in West Virginia, Montana, Ohio, and Pennsylvania, yielding a 53–47 majority to facilitate the incoming Trump administration’s agenda. Meanwhile, the GOP maintained a narrow majority in the U.S. House of Representatives, entering the 119th Congress with a 220–215 margin.

Your task is to transform today’s curated Reddit news feed (below) into a **Daily Briefing** that both parties can use to understand immediate crises and coordinate responses. The news feed are collected from one specific political subreddit, which may or may not be politically neutral. But your task is to synthesize all the news objectively by analyzing their importance, factual accuracy, and interpretation bias, considering their source domains, headlines, but **not** user engagements at this moment, as we are still developing that function.

You will be given today’s top posts — one JSON object per line, with creation ID, source domain, headline. The lines are strictly ranked based on article submission time to this subreddit. For example, the news coverage cycle is from 18:00 yesterday to 18:00 today. The first line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly after 18:00 yesterday. The last line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly before 18:00 today. After the precise moment that a political event happens, it takes an unspecified time delay, maybe as short as 15 minutes, maybe more than a day, for the political event to be submitted to the subreddit. But statistically, or on average, earlier events should be reported earlier in the subreddit than the time when later events are reported to the subreddit. We can't simply say, for example, that all the news stories in the second half of the day list, **happen** later than all the news stories in the first half of the day list, just because the second half is **reported** later. But when you randomly pick two stories, A and B, with A from the first half and B from the second half, the probability that B happens after A is higher than the probability that A happens after B. This heuristic method may be helpful for you to assemble news stories from fragmented news headlines. 

---

**You should produce a detailed briefing, following specific rules.**

Due to the complexity of the task, you should do this meticulously in multiple replies. In each reply you only do one step. You will only begin your Step 1 after you received all the JSON lines. There are 8 steps + 8 checks, 16 cycles.

The workflow is:

Step 1 (logic-heavy): Raw document given, define the categories of news
    First Check After Step 1
Step 2 (logic-heavy): Put Articles into Categories
    Sorting and First Check After Step 2
    Second Check After Step 2
Step 3 (logic-heavy): Scoring
    First Check After Step 3
Step 4 (logic-heavy): Sorting
    First Check After Step 4
    Second Check After Step 4
Step 5 (writing-heavy): Summarizing
    First Check After Step 5
Step 6 (writing-heavy): Composing
    First Check After Step 6
Step 7 (logic-heavy): Add the URLs
    First Check After Step 7
Step 8 (writing-heavy): Finalizing

You will keep editing a document which passes through multiple steps of processing. For each step, you only need to edit the document from my input or your last output. Let's define "a round of conversation" as my prompt + your output, basically my turn + your turn. Due to the sequential nature of the workflow, each step only depends on the introduction round, which is the very first round of our conversation, and our last two rounds of conversation, not anything in between. Therefore, to facilitate your multi-turn workflow, only the initial introduction round and the last two rounds of conversations will be provided to you as conversation history. In this way, your context length won't be exceeded, and you stay focus better. For each new round, please focus on the tasks defined in my latest prompt and build upon your output from your last two rounds. You also need to remember the background knowledge introduced in the first round.

You will be dealing with very long inputs and outputs. Please be very patient. You must do all the work and output everything in one go, no matter how long it is. But you can use your output as a part of your chain of thought. Just provide your final output after you finish your thinking.


**A very important rule is that factual accuracy is the utmost important issue. Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated, and you do not have Internet access right now.** You need to generate a report entirely based on the information provided in today's Reddit news headlines. Sometimes, a news headline may not give you enougn details to correctly interpret it. In this case, please do not make any speculation, and please report the unclear news headline exactly as it is, in quotes, and then remind the readers to check the source for details. 

That also applies to the titles and positions of political figures. Your internal knowledge is outdated. If the news headlines do not provide enough knowledge about the current title and position of a particular political figure, please do not add any title and position to that person, simply relying on your old knowledge. In this situation, if it doesn't feel critical, please skip the title and position, and directly use the full name of the person. If it does feel critical to mention the title and position of the person, please rely on the list of political figures as I provided earlier, but be aware that even that list may be a month behind reality. **Remember, when unsure, it is better to be vague than outright wrong.**

*   **Areas:** Scores reflect the aggregated importance and news volume of the topics within them. Areas containing multiple high-stakes topics (e.g., "The Epstein Case," "Executive Branch," and "State/Judicial Affairs") were rated as most important.

**CONFIDENTIAL DAILY BRIEFING**
**TO:** Congressional Leadership (D/R)
**FROM:** Chief News Analyst
**DATE:** July 19, 2025
**RE:** Unprecedented Executive Action and Resulting Crises

**OVERVIEW:**
This briefing synthesizes reporting on several rapidly escalating situations requiring immediate leadership attention. The dominant and most urgent crisis is the political fallout from the administration's handling of the Jeffrey Epstein files, which has triggered a significant intra-party rebellion within the President's base and is drawing intense public scrutiny. Concurrently, the administration is pursuing aggressive domestic and fiscal policies, including the potential removal of the Federal Reserve Chair and highly controversial actions by the Justice Department and ICE. These executive actions are drawing legal challenges from a coalition of states and are generating widespread public criticism. Internationally, the administration's tariff threats are prompting strategic realignments by key allies, and the pace of military air strikes has increased dramatically. In Congress, tensions are escalating as both parties prepare for high-stakes oversight investigations. This confluence of events presents a uniquely volatile and complex political environment.

He has publicly attacked followers focused on the case, calling them “stupid” and "weaklings," and has explicitly stated that he does not want their support if they continue to prioritize the matter [2, 3]. This aggressive posture comes even as some Republicans in Congress are reportedly pushing for more transparency in the probe, creating a potential rift between the White House and members of the GOP on Capitol Hill [4].

DAILY BRIEFING

**TO:** Congressional Leadership (D/R)
**FROM:** Chief News Analyst
**DATE:** July 19, 2025
**RE:** Unprecedented Executive Action and Resulting Crises

**OVERVIEW:**
This briefing synthesizes reporting on several rapidly escalating situations requiring immediate leadership attention. The dominant and most urgent crisis is the political fallout from the administration's handling of the Jeffrey Epstein files, which has triggered a significant intra-party rebellion within the President's base and is drawing intense public scrutiny. Concurrently, the administration is pursuing aggressive domestic and fiscal policies, including the potential removal of the Federal Reserve Chair and highly controversial actions by the Justice Department and ICE. These executive actions are drawing legal challenges from a coalition of states and are generating widespread public criticism. Internationally, the administration's tariff threats are prompting strategic realignments by key allies, and the pace of military air strikes has increased dramatically. In Congress, tensions are escalating as both parties prepare for high-stakes oversight investigations. This confluence of events presents a uniquely volatile and complex political environment.

---

## 1. The Epstein Case: Political & Legal Crisis

### 1.1 President Trump's Response and "Hoax" Allegations

President Trump is actively working to reframe the controversy over the Epstein files as a "hoax" and is directly confronting his own supporters on the issue. He has publicly attacked followers focused on the case, calling them “stupid” [1] and "weaklings," [2] and has explicitly stated that he does not want their support if they continue to prioritize the matter [3]. This aggressive posture comes even as some Republicans in Congress are reportedly pushing for more transparency in the probe, creating a potential rift between the White House and members of the GOP on Capitol Hill [4].

[1] Trump says people spreading ‘Epstein hoax’ are ‘stupid’, https://www.nbcnews.com/video/shorts/trump-says-people-spreading-epstein-hoax-are-stupid-243339333935  
[2] “I call it the Epstein hoax”: Trump attacks MAGA “weaklings” - President Donald Trump referred to the Epstein files as a "hoax" and said some of his supporters are "weaklings", https://www.salon.com/2025/07/16/i-call-it-the-epstein-hoax-trump-attacks-maga-weaklings/  
[3] Trump tells those focused on Epstein he doesn't want their support, https://www.politico.com/news/2025/07/16/trump-renounces-support-from-those-who-want-more-transparency-in-epstein-case-00455914  
[4] As Republicans call for transparency into Epstein probe, Trump lashes out, https://www.npr.org/2025/07/16/nx-s1-5469832/trump-epstein-doj

### 1.2 Intra-Party Conflict and Supporter Reactions

The President's stance has ignited what one report describes as a "MAGA Rebellion" that the administration is "frantically, failing" to crush [1]. Reporting from multiple outlets indicates the President's base is not "calming down" over the matter, with one headline quoting a source stating, "Is everyone calming down? 100% no" [2]. Prominent movement figures like Laura Loomer have warned the issue threatens to "consume" the Trump presidency entirely [3]. This conflict's intensity is highlighted by reports of a MAGA influencer who, after calling for a special counsel investigation, abruptly changed their position following the President's criticism [4].

### 1.3 Congressional Action and Calls for Document Release

House leadership is sending contradictory messages regarding the release of Epstein-related documents. Speaker Mike Johnson stated publicly that the GOP should "put everything out there" on the issue but subsequently voted against a measure to release the information [1]. In parallel, a resolution aimed at compelling Attorney General Pam Bondi to release the "Epstein Files" is reportedly "gaining steam" in the House, signaling growing pressure from within the legislative branch to force the administration's hand [2]. The division on this issue extends to specific delegations, with one report detailing how Florida representatives voted on the release measure [3].

This sentiment is reflected in what are described as "brutal" polling numbers for the President on this specific issue [2]. One political analysis frames the ongoing fallout as a potential "Achilles heel" for the president, suggesting a unique vulnerability not seen in previous controversies [3].

## 2. Executive Branch: Domestic Policy and Administration

### 2.1 Economic and Fiscal Policy

Significant scrutiny is being directed at the administration’s fiscal priorities and its relationship with the Federal Reserve. A report highlights the allocation of $300 million in public funds to help cover the costs of protecting Mar-a-Lago and Mr. Trump’s other private residences [1]. At the same time, President Trump has indicated he may fire Fed Chair Jerome Powell [2], a potential action that financial analysts are warning "would be a mess" for the economy [3]. The situation is compounded by reports that the President appeared surprised during a public appearance and seemed to forget that he had originally appointed Powell, instead blaming the previous administration for his continued presence as Fed Chair [4].

### 2.2 Justice Department and Federal Agency Conduct

The Justice Department is under a microscope following several actions perceived as politically motivated. The most prominent event is the firing of Maurene Comey—daughter of former FBI Director James Comey and the federal prosecutor who worked on the high-profile Ghislaine Maxwell and Sean 'Diddy' Combs cases [1]. This termination occurs amid reports of an ex-FBI official being "blocked" from investigating Trump’s Russia links [2] and as the President engages in what is described as a "pattern of political retribution" against opponents like Representative Adam Schiff [3]. Further reports detail a Trump official falsely accusing the PEPFAR foreign aid program of funding abortions in Russia [4].

The administration’s immigration enforcement policies are creating widespread controversy. Reports describe "chaotic" early days inside a new Florida detention center that has been nicknamed "Alligator Alcatraz" [1]. Immigration and Customs Enforcement (ICE) is a focal point of criticism, with one report alleging the agency denied a sitting member of Congress access to a detention facility [2]. In a separate development, ICE activity at a historic Japanese internment site is reported to be evoking the "painful legacy of incarceration" for local communities [3]. A further report details a Customs and Border Protection (CBP) policy that allows its agents to have gang-related tattoos, provided they are covered up while on duty [4].

Multiple states are taking direct action to oppose the administration's policies. A coalition of unnamed U.S. states is suing the Trump administration over its decision to cut disaster prevention grants [1]. In California, the state is establishing its own LGBTQ suicide prevention hotline after the federal government "announced it would no longer provide specialized support for LGBTQ+ youth on the national suicide prevention hotline" [3].

The administration has dramatically escalated the use of military force. A new analysis reveals that President Trump has authorized as many air strikes in his first five months in office as President Biden did over his entire four-year term [1]. Reporting on other defense policy changes is limited, though one headline alleges the administration is injecting "even more bigotry" into the military. The headline itself lacks specific details on the policy in question [2].
